# Fault Localization: NFS Mount Disappears Due to Inode Revalidate Failure

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/linux--07cc49f6 (mirror of torvalds/linux)
- **Kernel Version**: 4.1.15
- **Difficulty**: expert
- **Category**: fault_localization
- **Subsystem**: File System
- **Component**: NFS / SunRPC

## Bug Report

**Bug ID**: 117651
**Summary**: Root NFS and autofs - mount disappears due to inode revalidate failed
**Regression**: Yes (works on 3.14.12, broken on 4.1.15)

After upgrading from 3.14.12 to 4.1.15 I've got strange behaviour with autofs.

It happens on diskless machine with root on NFS. There is autofs indirect mount on /storage, where NFS volumes are mounted on demand.

Everything mounts normally, but after mount expiration (during unmount) autofs mount disappears - that is, not only /storage/<volume> unmounts, but /storage is also unmounted. This happens quite often - usually on the very first expiration.

automount logs umount error in such cases.

Without autofs, mount/umount of the same NFS volume works correctly.

With NFS debug enabled, I've got following errors:

```
NFS reply getattr: -512
nfs_revalidate_inode: (0:15/6291480) getattr failed, error=-512
NFS: nfs_lookup_revalidate(/storage) is invalid
```

After inode revalidate failure all mounts on this inode are unmounted and so autofs mount disappears, while automount daemon itself continue to run.

tcpdump shows, that server replies to getattr without error, but client doesn't see this reply, and returning error instead.

I am ready to supply additional information.

## Task

You are a fault localization agent. Given the bug report above, your task is to identify the **exact source file(s)** and **function(s)/data structure(s)** in the Linux kernel source tree (at `/workspace`) that need to be modified to fix this bug.

You must:
1. Analyze the bug report to understand the symptoms and context
2. Search the kernel source code to identify the relevant subsystem and files
3. Narrow down to the specific file(s) and function(s)/data structure(s) that contain the bug or need modification
4. Write your findings to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` in the following format:

```json
{
  "buggy_files": ["path/to/file.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["function_or_struct_name"],
  "confidence": 0.8,
  "reasoning": "Brief explanation of why these locations are the fault"
}
```

**Important**: Paths should be relative to the kernel source root (e.g., `kernel/sched/core.c`, not `/workspace/kernel/sched/core.c`).

## Success Criteria

- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy file(s)
- [ ] Correctly identify the buggy function(s) or data structure(s)
- [ ] Write results to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json`
- [ ] Provide reasoning for the localization

  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["nfs3_rpc_wrapper"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The nfs3_rpc_wrapper function (lines 30-42) is a wrapper around rpc_call_sync that handles -EJUKEBOX errors by retrying after a sleep. The bug is on line 39 where the code unconditionally sets 'res = -ERESTARTSYS' after calling freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() without checking the return value. This return value indicates whether the sleep was interrupted by a signal. When the sleep completes normally (no signal), res should remain -EJUKEBOX to allow the loop to retry the RPC call. Instead, the code unconditionally converts it to -ERESTARTSYS, which causes nfs_revalidate_inode to treat this as a permanent failure. This leads to inode invalidation even though the server may have successfully replied with the attributes. The tcpdump evidence in the bug report shows the server did reply, but the client incorrectly reports -512 (ERESTARTSYS) due to this race condition in the retry logic. The fix should check the return value of freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe and only set res = -ERESTARTSYS if a signal actually occurred."

{
  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/inode.c", "fs/nfs/dir.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["__nfs_revalidate_inode", "nfs_lookup_verify_inode"],
  "confidence": 0.82,
  "reasoning": "The bug is a failure to properly handle the -ERESTARTSYS (signal interrupted) error in the inode revalidation path. When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS. In __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c:960-971), this error is treated the same as other permanent errors - the function returns the error code without any special handling for this transient signal-based error. This error then propagates to nfs_lookup_verify_inode (fs/nfs/dir.c:1073-1075), which returns it to nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the dentry to be invalidated even though the inode itself is still valid. The tcpdump evidence shows the server DID reply successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before the reply could be fully processed and incorporated. The fix should treat -ERESTARTSYS as a transient, recoverable error: either retry the getattr call, or don't invalidate the inode/dentry when this error occurs. The root cause is that between kernels 3.14 and 4.1, the RPC/signal interaction changed such that signals can now interrupt getattr calls that previously wouldn't have been interrupted, exposing this missing error handling."
}

{
  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/inode.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["__nfs_revalidate_inode"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The bug is in __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c, lines 960-971) which fails to properly handle the -ERESTARTSYS error returned from NFS_PROTO(inode)->getattr(). When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS, which is a transient/recoverable error indicating 'try again' rather than a permanent failure. Currently, any non-zero status from getattr (lines 961-971) except -ESTALE is treated as a permanent error and returned to the caller, causing dentry invalidation in nfs_lookup_revalidate. This is incorrect for signal interruptions. The fix should add special handling for -ERESTARTSYS similar to -ESTALE: either retry the getattr or return 0 to indicate the inode remains valid despite the transient error. The tcpdump evidence in the bug report shows the server replied successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before fully processing the reply. Between kernel 3.14 and 4.1, changes to RPC signal handling made this race condition more likely, exposing the missing error handling."
}
---
6 /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
115-assistanttext-
Perfect! My fault localization analysis is complete. The issue has been identified in the NFS inode revalidation code where -ERESTARTSYS (signal-interrupted RPC calls) is incorrectly treated as a permanent error rather than a transient, recoverable one. 

## Summary

**Buggy File:** `fs/nfs/inode.c`

**Buggy Function:** `__nfs_revalidate_inode` (lines 960-971)

**Root Cause:** When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS, but this transient error is treated identically to permanent errors. This causes the inode to be invalidated incorrectly, leading to the entire mount point disappearing after autofs unmounts.

**Why It's a Regression:** Between kernel 3.14.12 and 4.1.15, changes to RPC signal handling made it more likely for getattr calls to be interrupted, exposing this missing error handling that was previously masked.

The result has been written to `/workspace/fault_localization_result.json` with confidence level 0.85.

When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS. In __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c:960-971), this error is treated the same as other permanent errors - the function returns the error code without any special handling for this transient signal-based error. This error then propagates to nfs_lookup_verify_inode (fs/nfs/dir.c:1073-1075), which returns it to nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the dentry to be invalidated even though the inode itself is still valid. The tcpdump evidence shows the server DID reply successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before the reply could be fully processed and incorporated. The fix should treat -ERESTARTSYS as a transient, recoverable error: either retry the getattr call, or don't invalidate the inode/dentry when this error occurs. The root cause is that between kernels 3.14 and 4.1, the RPC/signal interaction changed such that signals can now interrupt getattr calls that previously wouldn't have been interrupted, exposing this missing error handling.\"\n}",

        Code Changes (3)
        
1. WRITE /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
{
  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["nfs3_rpc_wrapper"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The nfs3_rpc_wrapper function (lines 30-42) is a wrapper around rpc_call_sync that handles -EJUKEBOX errors by retrying after a sleep. The bug is on line 39 where the code unconditionally sets 'res = -ERESTARTSYS' after calling freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() without checking the return value. This return value indicates whether the sleep was interrupted by a signal. When the sleep completes normally (no signal), res should remain -EJUKEBOX to allow the loop to retry the RPC call. Instead, the code unconditionally converts it to -ERESTARTSYS, which causes nfs_revalidate_inode to treat this as a permanent failure. This leads to inode invalidation even though the server may have successfully replied with the attributes. The tcpdump evidence in the bug report shows the server did reply, but the client incorrectly reports -512 (ERESTARTSYS) due to this race condition in the retry logic. The fix should check the return value of freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe and only set res = -ERESTARTSYS if a signal actually occurred."
}

2. EDIT /workspace/fault_localization_result.json
Before
{
  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["nfs3_rpc_wrapper"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The nfs3_rpc_wrapper function (lines 30-42) is a wrapper around rpc_call_sync that handles -EJUKEBOX errors by retrying after a sleep. The bug is on line 39 where the code unconditionally sets 'res = -ERESTARTSYS' after calling freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe() without checking the return value. This return value indicates whether the sleep was interrupted by a signal. When the sleep completes normally (no signal), res should remain -EJUKEBOX to allow the loop to retry the RPC call. Instead, the code unconditionally converts it to -ERESTARTSYS, which causes nfs_revalidate_inode to treat this as a permanent failure. This leads to inode invalidation even though the server may have successfully replied with the attributes. The tcpdump evidence in the bug report shows the server did reply, but the client incorrectly reports -512 (ERESTARTSYS) due to this race condition in the retry logic. The fix should check the return value of freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe and only set res = -ERESTARTSYS if a signal actually occurred."
}
After
{
  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/inode.c", "fs/nfs/dir.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["__nfs_revalidate_inode", "nfs_lookup_verify_inode"],
  "confidence": 0.82,
  "reasoning": "The bug is a failure to properly handle the -ERESTARTSYS (signal interrupted) error in the inode revalidation path. When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS. In __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c:960-971), this error is treated the same as other permanent errors - the function returns the error code without any special handling for this transient signal-based error. This error then propagates to nfs_lookup_verify_inode (fs/nfs/dir.c:1073-1075), which returns it to nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the dentry to be invalidated even though the inode itself is still valid. The tcpdump evidence shows the server DID reply successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before the reply could be fully processed and incorporated. The fix should treat -ERESTARTSYS as a transient, recoverable error: either retry the getattr call, or don't invalidate the inode/dentry when this error occurs. The root cause is that between kernels 3.14 and 4.1, the RPC/signal interaction changed such that signals can now interrupt getattr calls that previously wouldn't have been interrupted, exposing this missing error handling."
}

When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS. In __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c:960-971), this error is treated the same as other permanent errors - the function returns the error code without any special handling for this transient signal-based error. This error then propagates to nfs_lookup_verify_inode (fs/nfs/dir.c:1073-1075), which returns it to nfs_lookup_revalidate, causing the dentry to be invalidated even though the inode itself is still valid. The tcpdump evidence shows the server DID reply successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before the reply could be fully processed and incorporated. The fix should treat -ERESTARTSYS as a transient, recoverable error: either retry the getattr call, or don't invalidate the inode/dentry when this error occurs. After

  "buggy_files": ["fs/nfs/inode.c"],
  "buggy_functions": ["__nfs_revalidate_inode"],
  "confidence": 0.85,
  "reasoning": "The bug is in __nfs_revalidate_inode (fs/nfs/inode.c, lines 960-971) which fails to properly handle the -ERESTARTSYS error returned from NFS_PROTO(inode)->getattr(). When an RPC getattr call is interrupted by a signal, it returns -ERESTARTSYS, which is a transient/recoverable error indicating 'try again' rather than a permanent failure. Currently, any non-zero status from getattr (lines 961-971) except -ESTALE is treated as a permanent error and returned to the caller, causing dentry invalidation in nfs_lookup_revalidate. This is incorrect for signal interruptions. The fix should add special handling for -ERESTARTSYS similar to -ESTALE: either retry the getattr or return 0 to indicate the inode remains valid despite the transient error. The tcpdump evidence in the bug report shows the server replied successfully, but the client task was interrupted by a signal before fully processing the reply. Between kernel 3.14 and 4.1, changes to RPC signal handling made this race condition more likely, exposing the missing error handling."
